рдЕрде рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ тАШ рдХ рдИрдВ рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╕рд┐рд╖реНрдард╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдорд░реБрджреНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдореН ред рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛ рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдГ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХрд╛рдиреНрддрдВ– рдХ рдИрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╛ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рд╣рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛ рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрджрд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рджрд╢рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗрд╜рд╣рдиреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд╛рд░реБрддреЗ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдЗрджрдВ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░реНрдпрддреЗ рд╣рд┐ – рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрдорддреМ рдХ рдИрдВ рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддрд╛ рдирд░рдГ ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рео. рео) рдЗрддрд┐ редред

Jamison Brereton

56 (572)
Maruts
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
25 verses: dvipad─Б vir─Бj 1тАУ11, triс╣гс╣нubh 12тАУ25
This hymn is structured like VII.34, an All God hymn, in that the first part is in the short dvipad─Б meter and the second part in triс╣гс╣нubh, although the proportions of verses in each meter are different. It also shares a final verse with VII.34, a generic plea for the godsтАЩ protection. But in content there is little in common between the two hymns.
This hymn begins with four verses about the birth and identity of the Maruts, alluding both to their mysterious generation from Pr╠е┼Ыni (see esp. vs. 4) and the para dox that they are both identical (тАЬbelonging to the same nest,тАЭ vs. 1) and separate and rivalrous. This theme then disappears from the hymn, save for several refer ences to their plural тАЬnamesтАЭ (vss. 10, 14; we of course know them only under one name, тАЬMarutsтАЭ). The rest of the dvipad─Б section (vss. 5тАУ11) is essentially descrip tive, of their power, beauty, and accoutrements.
Although this celebration of the MarutsтАЩ qualities continues in the triс╣гс╣нubh por tion, there is also a significant ritual component, initiated in the first half of verse 12. Subsequent verses make clear what ritual is involved: in verse 14 it is said that they are worshiped at the beginning of the sacrifice, and they are invited to enjoy the House-offering; in verse 16 they are called тАЬplayful.тАЭ In middle Vedic ritual the third and last of the тАЬFour-monthlyтАЭ (C─Бturm─Бsy─Бni) rituals is the S─Бkamedha, celebrated in the autumn. On the day before the S─Бkamedha day proper, the Maruts receive two oblationsтАФthus, they are worshiped at the beginning of the sacrifice. Moreover, the second of these two oblations is the тАЬHouse-offeringтАЭ (Gr╠еhamedh─лya). And on the next day there is an offering to the тАЬplayful Maruts,тАЭ using the same word that describes their behavior in verse 16d. (For further refer
ence to the Maruts at the S─Бkamedha in this Marut cycle, see VII.59.9тАУ10. On the ritual itself see, e.g., Hillebrandt 1897: 117тАУ19; Keith 1925: 322тАУ23.) As usual, offerings to the gods prompt us to ask for reciprocal benefits from the gods, and these requests occupy much of the remaining verses (17тАУ24), with the final refrain verse (25) extending the requests to other gods as well. The last few request verses specific to the Maruts (vss. 22тАУ24) ask for their help in battles over land and waters, alluding presumably to the ─Аrya expansion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho are these resplendent chiefs, the dwellers in one abode, the sons of Rudra, friends of man, atpresent well-mounted?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who, separately, are these anointed superior men who belong to the same nestтАФ
the young bloods of Rudra, possessing good horses?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes cd to be the answer to the question in ab, but since vs. 2 seems more directly responsive to the question, I take cd here as simply further specification of the subject of the question.

Unusually, ─лm has no acc. function; there is no possible accusative role it could fill.

I consider vy├аkt─Б(s) to be at least an implied pun. The first reading is as the nom. pl. m. of the ppl. of v├н тИЪa├▒j тАШanoint, ornamentтАЩ, referring presumably to the MarutsтАЩ characteristic adornments and their glistening appearance as (wet) bearers of rain. This interpr. is reflected in all the standard tr. However, I think it also is meant to contrast with s├бn─лс╕╖─Бс╕е тАШof the same nestтАЩ, as an indication that the Maruts are also separate individuals, and employing the common v├н / s├б(m) polarization. The problem is to identify a morphological form that could be represented by vy├аkt─Б(s) and express the sense тАШseparate, individualтАЩ vel sim. I hesitantly suggest that we start with the -a├▒c-stem, vy-├б├▒c-, found only in the cmpd. uru-vy├б├▒c- тАШwide-spreadingтАЩ.

(The rarity of this stem may be accounted for by competition with the well-attested stem v├нс╣гva├▒c- of almost the same meaning [тАШfacing in opposite directions, divergentтАЩ], which looks like a more substantial version of vy├б├▒c- and is built to the extended form v├нс╣гu of the same preverb v├н.) If vy├б├▒c- made a collective abstract in -t─Б-,

*vy├бkt─Б- тАШindividuality, separatenessтАЩ, the form in our passage could be its instr. sg.

in adverbial usage. There are obviously weaknesses in every link in this chain of reasoning. First, the stem vy├б├▒c- is very rare and limited in distribution; second, I know of no other such abstracts to -a├▒c-stems and in fact -t─Б-stems are relatively rare in early Vedic (AiG II.2.617); third, it should be accented *vy├б├▒c- (AiG II.2.619).

However, a poet intent on packing a pun into vy├аkt─Б(s) might not scruple to use unusual forms to achieve it, and elsewhere in the RV puns sometimes ignore accentuation for their 2nd reading. In slight support of the suggestion, we might note that this set of hymns has one other ex. of the instr. of such a stem in adverbial usage:

Griffith

Wno are these radiant men in serried rank, Rudra’s young heroes borne by noble steeds?

Geldner

Wer sind die aufgeputzten gleichb├╝rtigen Mannen? Die J├╝nglinge des Rudra und gute Reiter!

Grassmann

Wer sind die sch├╢nen тАУ vereinten M├дnner, Des Rudra Mannen тАУ mit sch├╢nen Rossen?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNo one indeed knows their origin, they alone respectively know their birth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For no one knows their (separate) births.
But certainly they know, mutually, each his own separate means of
begetting.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. seems a response, if an indirect one, to the question posed in vs. 1.

The h├н, as often, has a higher discourse function: it gives the reason for asking the question in the first place. We could tr. тАЬ(I ask) because тАжтАЭ I also consider this vs. a further expression of the тАЬindividual/collectiveтАЭ theme I identified in vs. 1, here 80 conveyed by the pl. jan┼л╠Бс╣Гс╣гi тАШbirthsтАЩ in the first clause, contrasted with the sg.

jan├нtram тАШmeans of begettingтАЩ in the 2nd. If 1ab asks тАЬwho are they individually?тАЭ 2ab states that the question needs to be asked because no one knows their individual births, even though (cd) they [=Maruts] know тАЬmutuallyтАЭ (mith├бс╕е) their own (individual) means of begetting. In other words, they share the knowledge of their separate births – something we donтАЩt know. Note the middle vidre: they know facts about themselves, contrasting with the 3rd-party lack of knowledge in ab n├бkiс╕е тАж v├йda.

Griffith

Verily no one knoweth whence they sprang: they, and they only, know each other’s birth.

Geldner

Denn keiner kennt ihre Abkunft; sie allein kennen gegenseitig ihren Ursprung.

Grassmann

Denn ihren Ursprung тАУ erkennt kein andrer, Sie selbst nur kennen тАУ die eigne Abkunft.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey go together by their own pure paths; roaring like the wind, and fleet as falcons, they mutually rivaleach other.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They sprinkled each other mutually, each with his own self-purifying (rain drops? semen?).
The falcons with the windтАЩs roar contended among themselves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. continues the theme of mutuality in vs. 2, but now concerns the MarutsтАЩ adult behavior as gods of the storm. The mutuality is expressed both by the adv. mith├бс╕е repeated from vs. 2 and by the reciprocal 3rd pl. verb aspс╣Ыdhran тАЬthey contended with each other.тАЭ The hapax svap┼л╠Б- has been variously, and surprisingly, interpr. See Oldenberg ad loc. (also KEWA s.v., etc.) for the numerous suggestions, incl. BR тАШbroomтАЩ, Lanman тАШwingsтАЩ. However, the most obvious analysis also is most likely the correct one, as a root noun cmpd. to root тИЪp┼л тАШpurifyтАЩ, hence тАШself-purifyingтАЩ. This is OldenbergтАЩs conclusion, reflected also in GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs tr. and in Scarlatta (323). Perhaps the resistance to this obvious interpr. resulted from the fact that it is a hapax – astonishing given the centrality of Soma Pavam─Бna тАЬself-purifying SomaтАЭ in RVic ritual as the subject of the entire IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala – and in this passage it has no connection with soma. Here it quite likely refers to the rain drops accompanying the MarutsтАЩ storm, as Geldner suggests.

Oldenberg acutely notes that the verb in this p─Бda vapanta resembles pavanta тАШthey purify(/ied) themselvesтАЩ. Rather than considering vapanta a corruption of pavanta (which seems extremely unlikely to me), I would instead suggest that itтАЩs a metathetic word play (vap тЙИ pav), aided by preceding (s)vap(┼л╠Бbhiс╕е).

Griffith

They strew each other with their blasts, these Hawks: they strove together, roaring like the wind.

Geldner

Mit ihren eigenen Reinigungsmitteln besch├╝tten sie sich gegenseitig. Die wie der Wind rauschenden Falken sind in Wettstreit geraten.

Grassmann

Mit Licht bestreuen тАУ sie selbst einander, Die Adler k├дmpften тАУ wie Winde brausend.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe sage may know those white-complexioned beings (the Maruts), whom the vast Pс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зi born at herudder.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

White-complexioned: et─Бni ninya = ┼Ыveta varс╣З─Бni bh┼лt─Бni marut─Бtmak─Бni, white-coloured beings,identical with the Maruts; bore at her udder: udho babh─Бra: udhas = firmament of the womb

Jamison Brereton

These are the secrets the insightful one perceives:
what great Pr╠е┼Ыni bore as her udder.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Whenever the birth of the Maruts, and esp. the udder of Pс╣Ы┼Ыni, are found in the RV, bewilderment ensues, and this passage is no exception. At least it is here identified as a secret that only the insightful can perceive – a characterization that the modern interpreter fully concurs with. For other problematic passages on this topic see II.34.2, VI.48.22, and VI.66.1, 3 with comm. ad locc. Our passage would be fairly easy to interpr. if we could take ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е (that is, ┼л╠Бdhar) as a loc. sg. Such is GeldnerтАЩs solution (тАЬim Euter,тАЭ explicitly identified as a loc. in n. 4b) and also RenouтАЩs, though the latter has the grace to bury the loc. in a parenthesis: тАЬ(en sa) mamelle.тАЭ But a loc. -ar to r/n stems тАЬist nicht nachgewiesenтАЭ (AiG III.311), and it is safer to take it as an acc. sg. as elsewhere. In my interpr. y├бd is a neut. pronoun (rather than a subord. conj.) and refers collectively to the Maruts and тАШudderтАЩ is a species of appositive to it though with a bit of a twist: тАШudderтАЩ refers to the contents of the udder, and that contents is the collective Marut embryo(s). This seems to me better than taking y├бd as тАШthatтАЩ or the like, as in K├╝mmelтАЩs (175) тАЬDiese Geheimnisse kennt der Weise, dass die grosse Pr┼Ы╠е ni ein Euter getragen hat.тАЭ (On p. 339 K├╝mmel simply reproduces GeldnerтАЩs tr., with ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е as loc. and a pronominal obj. [тАЬsieтАЭ], referring to the Maruts, supplied; he doesnтАЩt comment on these two incompatible interpr.) 81

Griffith

A sage was he who knew these mysteries, what in her udder mighty Prsni bore.

Diese Geheimnisse kennt der Weise, da├Я die gro├Яe Prisni sie im Euter getragen hat.

Doch dies Geheimniss тАУ erkennt der Weise, Dass bot ihr Euter тАУ die grosse Pri├зni.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the people, through (the favours of) the Maruts, always victorious, possessed of male posterity,and in the enjoyment of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let this clan be possessed of good heroes in (the form of) Maruts, the clan prevailing from of old, fostering its manly power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The good heroes that the clan possesses are in fact the Maruts themselves, specified in the instr. Renou calls this an тАЬinstrumental of identification.тАЭ Whatever term is used, it is not, in my experience, a common usage of the instr., but it is nonetheless not hard to interpret. A similar usage is found two vss. later, in 7cd.

Griffith

Ever victorious, through the Maruts, be this band of Heroes, nursing manly strength,

Geldner

Dieser Clan mu├Я durch die Marut heldenhaft sein, von jeher siegend, an Mannesst├дrke zunehmend.

Grassmann

Dies Volk der Helden, тАУ durch Maruts sei es F├╝r immer siegreich тАУ und Mannheit erntend.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe Maruts rapidly repair to the plural ce (of their destination), richly decorated with ornaments, investedwith beauty, terrible by their strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Best driving their drive, most beautiful in beauty, supplied with splendor, strong with strengthsтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

A very cleverly constructed vs., nicely fitted to Dvipad─Б Vir─Бj meter. Each 5-syl. p─Бda consists of two words, phonologically and etymologically (or pseudoetymologically) related. There are both repetition of morphological figures and variation on them. All four p─Бdas end with a nom. pl. masc. adj.; the first two p─Бdas end with superlative -iс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е, the third with the phonologically similar, but morphologically distinct -i┼Ыl─Б(с╕е), the last with something phonologically distinct (ugr─Б╠Бс╕е).

Three (a, b, d) of the four p─Бdas contain etymological pairs; in the first two the etymological relation is reinforced by phonological repetition (y─Б╠Бmaс╣Г y─Б╠Б(y)iс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е, ┼Ыubh─Б╠Б┼Ы├│bhiс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е. (As for the first, the Saс╣Гh. has y├йс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Бс╕е, but the first vowel must be distracted. Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition restore y├бyiс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е with short root vowel, but I think y─Б is more likely.

In neither of the other two occurrences of this stem [V.41.3, 74.8] does the meter establish the quantity of the root syllable.) In the third ex. (p─Бda d) the etymological relationship is not transparent, but would be available to the audience steeped in derivational morphology: ├│jobhir ugr─Б╠Бс╕е. Although c, ┼Ыriy─Б╠Бs├бmmi┼Ыl─Б╠Б(с╕е), lacks the etymological connection, it mimics it through alliteration, though it is notable that we have mi┼ЫLa, not the also attested mi┼ЫRa, which would match ┼Ыriy─Б╠Бbetter. Another set of three versus one: in three p─Бdas (b, c, d) the first noun is in the instr., but in p─Бda a it is not. The 2nd p─Бda is the only one that doesnтАЩt deviate from the various patterns in any regard: itтАЩs an etymological figure, ends with a superlative, begins with an instrumental.

One can also note the reversal of vowels in the root syllables of the word pairs of b and d: u тАж o versus o тАж u.

Most bright in splendour, flectest on their way, close-knit to glory, strong with varied power.

English translation:

тАЬTerrible be your strength, steadfast your energies, prosperous be the company of the Maruts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Strong is your strength, steadfast your forces. Thus the flock with its Maruts is powerful.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda of this vs., ugr├бс╣Г va ├│jaс╕е, restates the last p─Бda of the preceding vs. (6d ├│jobhir ugr─Б╠Бс╕е) as an equational nominal clause. Because of its connection with vs. 6 it also sets up the expectation that what follows will also be an etymological figure, but b sthir─Б╠Б┼Ы├бv─Бс╣Гsi is not, though it has the same syntactic configuration as p─Бda a.

The loose construction of the instr. mar├║dbhiс╕е is similar to that in 5a.

Griffith

Yea, mighty is your power and firm your strength: so, potent, with the Maruts, be the band.

Geldner

Stark ist eure St├дrke, fest die Macht, und durch die Marut ist die Schar kraftvoll.

Grassmann

Gewalt’ge Kraft euch тАУ und feste Sehnen, Und eure Heerschar тАУ an Maruts zahlreich.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorious is your vigour, unrelenting are your minds; (the exertion) of your irresistible force, the agitator(of the trees), is like (the manifold tone of the prayers of) a muni.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Manifold tone: dhuni muniriva = the agitationlike a muni; the sounds produced by the shaking of the trees are like the varied intonations of a reciter ofpraises

Jamison Brereton

Beautiful is your bluster, raging are the minds of the bold troop, like a raving ecstatic.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The nominal equations of 7ab continue in the first half of this vs., and ┼Ыubhr├бс╕е picks up ┼Ыubh─Б╠Б┼Ы├│bhiс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е of 6b. Although ┼Ы├║с╣гmaс╕е is not etymologically related to ┼Ыubhr├бс╕е, they are alliterative.

P─Бda c contains a rhyming simile: dh├║nir m├║nir. Such full rhyme is quite rare in the RV and seems to provide the crescendo of this highly wrought little passage.

Note also that the final of d, dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├│с╕е, is a slight flip of the initial of c, dh├║niс╕е. 82 In order to get a proper Dvipad─Б Vir─Бj line, the iva of c has to be read тАШva, as it sometimes is elsewhere. See Oldenberg If the particle is disyllabic, however, it makes cd a Triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda. Since the Dvipad─Б Vir─Бj section of the hymn is drawing to a close (fully Triс╣гtubh starting with vs. 12), the possible double metrical reading here may be gesturing towards the upcoming Triс╣гс╣нubh takeover. Indeed the Dvipad─Б Vir─Бj begins to break up beginning in vs. 10, despite the Anukr. identification of 1-11 as DV.

In the simile of c, iva (/va) is out of place; we expect *dh├║nir iva m├║niс╕е. This displacement was doubtless made to draw attention to the rhyme noted above. But it also interacts somewhat with the question of whether cd contains two DV p─Бdas or one Triс╣гс╣нubh, because a quick glance at Lubotsky shows that iva is fairly rare immediately after the caesura, which would be its position here if we are dealing with a Triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda. I imagine that this rarity has less to do with ivaтАЩs accentless status (though that might contribute) than with its usual tendency to take 2nd position, which would generally put it earlier in the line. There certainly do exist trimeter lines with iva post-caesura, e.g., IV.18.6 с╣Ыt─Бvar─лr iva saс╣Гkr├│с╣гam─Бn─Бс╕е (cf. also V.1.1, 11.5, etc.); they are just less common than I had expected.

Griffith

Bright is your spirit, wrathful are your minds: your bold troop’s minstrel is like one inspired.

English translation:

тАЬI invoke your beloved names, Maruts, destroyers (of foes), that they who are desirous of the offeringmay be satisfied.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I call the dear names of you precipitate ones,
when you are here bellowing to your heartsтАЩ content, o Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The metrical decay noted for 8cd continues here. Although the first half of the vs. has the expected 10 syllables with a word boundary after 5 – thus allowing a division into two DV p─Бdas – the opening of b is huve, an unaccented verb. In the immediately preceding vs. p─Бda b opens with accented yuy├│ta, which must owe its accent to its p─Бda-initial position, as there are no syntactic features favoring it. The DV here is far less sensitive to the p─Бda boundary. Even more clearly, the second half of the vs. is an undoubted Triс╣гс╣нubh, since it has 11 syllables and a caesura after the first 4, with the unaccented voc. maruto spanning syllables 5-7.

Both Geldner and Renou (also Lubotsky) take v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е to тИЪva┼Ы тАШwant, desireтАЩ with the supposed object being soma, but I think it makes more sense, and requires less machinery, to assign it to тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ. Otherwise too much has been gapped and needs to be supplied; cf. RenouтАЩs expansive parenthesis: тАЬтАж pour quтАЩ├а sati├йt├й тАж (vous vous gorgiez de soma, le) d├йsirant-avec-force.тАЭ See the same disagreement about the affiliation of the same participle in VII.36.6, with comm. ad loc.

Griffith

Your dear names, conquering Maruts, we invoke, calling aloud till we are satisfied.

Geldner

Euer, der Hochstehenden, liebe Namen rufe ich an, auf da├Я ihr Marut euch gierig zur Gen├╝ge mit Soma begie├Яet;

Grassmann

Ich rufe eure тАУ der raschen Namen, Dass ihr begier’gen тАУ euch labt, o Maruts.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBearers are (the Maruts) of bright weapons, rapid are they in motion, wearers of brilliant ornaments,and self-radiators of their person ns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They are possessed of good weapons and arrows, of lovely
neck-ornaments,
and are themselves beautifying their own bodies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is unambiguously Triс╣гс╣нubh, consisting of two p─Бdas of 11 syllables. The first has an opening of 5, which could be a self-contained p─Бda of DV, but what follows it is 6 syllables, marking the whole as a single Triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda. The second part is even less ambiguous, as it has an opening of 4, so a DV division is impossible. The only feature that matches that of DV is that there are only two Triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бdas in the vs., not four.

On iс╣гm├нn- see comm. ad I.87.6.

Well-armed, impetuous in their haste, they deck themselves, their forms, with oblations: to you, the pure, ornaments made of gold.

English translation:

тАЬPure oblations be offered, Maruts, to you who are pure; the shedders of water proceed by truth to truth,pure, purifying, of pure birth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Gleaming are the oblations for you gleaming ones, o Maruts. I set in motion a gleaming ceremonial course for the gleaming ones.
By truth the servers of truth came to realityтАФthe gleaming ones of gleaming birth, pure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The metrical boundary, however fuzzy, between the DV and Triс╣гс╣нubh sections separates the first part of the hymn from the more ritually focused one 83 beginning here. The expression hinomy adhvar├бm тАЬI set the ceremony in motionтАЭ announces the inauguration of the sacrifice.

This vs. harps, rather tediously, on the adj. ┼Ы├║ci- тАШgleamingтАЩ, which occurs 6x, twice each in p─Бdas a, b, and d.

P─Бda c contrasts с╣Ыt├б- in с╣Ыt├йna тАж с╣Ыta-s─Б╠Бpaс╕е with saty├б-, the latter as goal of тИЪi тАШgo, comeтАЩ. In my view, saty├бm тАж ─Бyan refers to the truth-serving MarutsтАЩ epiphany on the ritual ground: they тАЬcame to realityтАЭ for the sacrificers, that is, they became really present. This epiphany is effected тАЬby truthтАЭ: the operation of the properly performed ritual mechanism.

Griffith

Pure, Maruts, pure yourselves, are your oblations: to you, the pure, pure sacrifice I offer.
By Law they came to truth, the Law’s observers, bright by their birth, and pure, and sanctifying.

Geldner

Rein sind die Opfergaben f├╝r euch, die Reinen, o Marut; ein reines Opfer bringe ich f├╝r die Reinen in Gang. Nach dem Gesetz das Gesetz wahrend gingen sie in die Welt der Wahrheit ein, von reiner Geburt, die Reinen, Lauteren.

Grassmann

Hell sind die G├╝sse, Maruts, euch den hellen ich r├╝ste helles Opferwerk den hellen; Die hellgebornen hellen kamen flammend, gelockt durch Opfer, wahrhaft Opfer liebend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBright ornaments, Maruts, are on your shoulders, shining (necklaces) are pendant on your breasts,glittering with rain, like lightnings, you are distributing the waters with your weapons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bright ornaments:kh─Бdayo alaс╣Еk─Бra vi┼Ыeс╣гaс╕е: kh─Бdi, a guard of the hand (RV. 1.23.4.3); Maruts are bearers of lances on theirshoulders; shining necklaces: rukma = rocam─Бna, shining; elsewhere Maruts are said to have golden cuirasseson their breasts; possibly rukma may mean the same

Jamison Brereton

On your shoulders, Maruts, are spangles, on your breasts brilliants are being set.
Like lightning flashes shining forth with the rains, (you are) holding yourselves ready with your weapons according to your nature.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. has no finite verbs, but three predicated tense-stem participles: pf.

upa┼Ыi┼Ыriy─Бс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е (b), aor. ruc─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е (c), pres. y├бcham─Бn─Бс╕е (d), in a hymn already well provided with such (see 10d, 11d).

As for upa┼Ыi┼Ыriy─Бс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е, although pf. participles regularly have preterital value, the middle pf. of тИЪ┼Ыri is presential (K├╝mmel 527-28) and stative, and this form contrasts with the far more common ppl. ┼Ыrita- тАШsetтАЩ – hence my тАЬbeing set,тАЭ though this rendering somewhat undercuts the stative value.

In cd it is possible that only one of the participles is predicated, and in fact the published translation renders p─Бda c as wholly a simile. However, this hemistich could contain two independent predications: тАЬ(you are) shining like тАж; (you are) holding yourselves тАжтАЭ In any case there is an unsignaled change of subject between the hemistichs: in ab the ornaments (nom. kh─Бd├бyaс╕е, rukm─Б╠Бс╕е) are the grammatical subjects, while in d the Maruts must be supplied because the participle y├бcham─Бn─Бс╕е seems to assume an animate subject. P─Бda c is ambiguous: either the brilliants (rukm─Б╠Бс╕е) or the Maruts can be shining. The etymological relationship between rukm─Б╠Бс╕е in b and the part. ruc─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е in c might suggest that c goes with b. However, in my published translation I have privileged the hemistich boundary and supplied the Maruts as subj.

of c (as do Geldner and Renou), but the other interpr. is certainly possible. One argument for the standard interpr. might be that the subjects of medial participles to тИЪruc (wellattested r├│cam─Бna-, as well as ruc─Бn├б-, ruruc─Бn├б-, r├│ruc─Бna-) are generally gods.

Griffith

Your rings, O Maruts, rest upon your shoulders, and chains of gold are twined upon your bosoms.
Gleaming with drops of rain, like lightning-flashes, after your wont ye whirl about your weapons.

Geldner

Auf euren Schultern, ihr Marut, sind Spangen, an eurer Brust ist Goldschmuck angesteckt. Sie gl├дnzen wie Blitze im Regen, mit den Waffen ihrer Eigenart entsprechend.

Grassmann

An euren Schultern, Maruts, gl├дnzen Spangen, mit Goldschmuck habt ihr eure Brust bekleidet, Wie helle Blitze unter Regen funkelnd, nach eigner Weise eure Waffen schwingend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour celestial splendours, Maruts, spread wide; objects of worship, you send down (the waters) thatbeat down (the dust); accept Maruts, this your portion of the domestic worship of the household multiplied athousand-fold.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Waters that beat down the dust: n─Бm─Бni tiradhvam p─Бс╣Гs┼лn namayanti n─Бm─Бni udak─Бni:n─Бm─Бni = waters, for they bend down the dust; multipled a thousand- fold: How can one portion become athousand? The quantity of an offering is computed, not by its actual number, but by that assigned to it by thedivinity to whom it is offered, y─Бvad ek─Б devat─Б k─Бmayate y─Бvadeka t─Бvad ─Бhutiс╕е prathate

Jamison Brereton

Your deep-grounded great powers rise forth. Set forth your names, you who are worshiped at the forefront of the sacrifice.
Enjoy this thousandfold domestic portion of the House-offering, o Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner suggests (n. 14a) that the budhny─Б╠АтАж m├бh─Бс╣Гsi тАЬdeep-grounded powersтАЭ are the тАЬverborgenen HerrlichkeitenтАЭ (niс╣Зy─Б╠Б) concealed in Pс╣Ы┼ЫniтАЩs udder in vs. 4. Even leaving aside the fact that, as was discussed above, ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е in vs. 4 should not be a loc., this interpr. seems both unnec. and too specific, esp. since 10 vss.

intervene. budhny├а- here may refer to the powers that the Maruts, gods associated with the midspace, derive from the earth below, or it may simply mean something like тАШfundamentalтАЩ, by a semantic development parallel to that of the Engl. word.

The preverb pr├б is showcased in the first hemistich: pr├б тАж ─лrate тАж, pr├б тАж prayajyavas tiradhvam. I am not certain what pr├б тИЪtс╣Э n─Б╠Бm─Бni in b is meant to convey, but I interpr. it in the context of the importance of the MarutsтАЩ individual identities (vss. 1-4) and of calling their names (10a) earlier in the hymn. Perhaps the Maruts need to тАЬput their names forwardтАЭ and make themselves individually known before they can enjoy the Gс╣Ыhamedha offering. 84 As noted in the published introduction, the ritual references in p─Бdas b-d are quite specific, alluding to the MarutsтАЩ role in the S─Бkamedha, the last of the C─Бturm─Бsy─Бni (тАЬFour-monthlyтАЭ) rituals. See the published introduction. for further details.

Griffith

Wide in the depth of air spread forth your glories, far, most adorable, ye bear your titles.
Maruts, accept this thousandfold allotment of household sacrifice and household treasure.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf, Maruts, you justly appreciate the praise of the devout offerer of (sacrificial) food, conjoined withoblations, then promptly bestow (upon us) riches, comprehending excellent male posterity, such as no unfriendlyman can take away.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If, Maruts, you give study to what is praised in just this way at the invocation of the prizewinning inspired poet,
right away give of wealth consisting of heroes, which another man, a non-giver, will never swindle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phonological figure of the two words adh─лth├б, itth─Б╠Бstraddling the p─Бda boundary of ab provide a nice little study in syllable weight. (The echo is of course obscured by the application of sandhi in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text: adh─лth├йth─Б╠Б). If we add in the opening of the vs., y├бdi, the echo is even more pronounced: y├бdi тАж adh─лth├б, itth─Б╠Б, with (y)├бdi doubling adh─л.

Exactly what itth─Б╠Бis doing here is unclear to me, but this adverb several times appears in context with v├нpra- and some verb of invoking (see Geldner ad VII.94.5), as here (with the invoking represented by the nominal h├бv─лman). Cf. VII.94.5 тАж ─лс╕╖ata, itth─Б╠Бv├нpr─Бsaс╕е, IV.29.4 = VIII.7.30 itth─Б╠Бv├нpraс╣Г h├бvam─Бnam. I suggest that itth─Б╠Б refers to the precise manner in which a v├нpra- makes the invocation.

The Maruts are asked to тАЬgive study to / be mindful ofтАЭ what is stut├бsya.

stut├б- is of course a very common past passive participle meaning тАШ(what/who is) praisedтАЩ. In this context we might rather expect the abstract noun тАШpraiseтАЩ, and indeed Geldner simply so tr.: тАЬтАж des Lobpreises eingedenk seid,тАЭ with no explicit comment, but a crossref. (n. 15a) to several passages with a similar idiom but with stotr├бsya тАШpraise songтАЩ instead of stut├бsya (e.g., V.55.9 ├бdhi st├│trasya тАж g─Бtana). But the poet could easily have used stotr├бsya here in the same metrical slot if he had wanted to, and so I think we must take the ppl. seriously. Renou in fact does so – тАЬpr├кtez-attention ├а la chose-lou├йeтАЭ – though in his n. he simply notes its similarity to the stotr├б- passages.

I think the point is a cleverer one: the poet suggests that if the Maruts pay attention to what we poets praise – what gifts we poets praise – they will know what to bestow on us. The тАЬifтАЭ clause is immediately followed by its corollary: тАЬright away give (us) wealth тАжтАЭ – the poet implying that the Maruts are a quick study! Although I must admit that stut├б- тАШpraisedтАЩ seems always to refer to gods, not to material objects, the semantic extension seems an easy one, and we can invoke the term d─Бna-stuti- тАШpraise of the giftтАЩ - though itтАЩs notable that, although this term is ubiquitous in secondary lit. on the RV, it is not actually attested in Vedic.

By my rules, we might expect that any├бс╕е in d should be definite (тАШthe otherтАЩ) rather than the indefinite тАШanotherтАЩ that better fits the passage (unless we assume that the any├бс╕е is a rival poet). However, I suggest that n┼л╠Бcid тАж any├бс╕е is a composite negative indefinite expression like n├б k├б┼Ы cid any├бh. Cf. VIII.24.11 n┼л╠Бany├бtr─Б cid тАж The cadence of d is bad. It is tempting to emend injunc. ─Бd├бbhat to subj.

─Бd├бbh─Бt, which would fix the meter and fit the sense (in fact, the published translation renders the verb as if a subj.: тАШwill тАж swindleтАЩ), though no doubt the temptation should be resisted.

Griffith

If, Maruts, ye regard the praise recited here at this mighty singer invocation,
Vouchsafe us quickly wealth with noble heroes, wealth which no man uho hateth us may injure.

Geldner

Wenn ihr Marut des Lobpreises eingedenk seid, da der Redekundige sieggekr├╢nte S├дnger also ruft, so gebet alsbald einen Schatz von Meistern, den niemals ein anderer Mi├Яg├╝nstiger hintergehen soll!

Grassmann

Wenn wirklich ihr des Lobs gedenkt, o Maruts, bei dem Gebet des opferreichen S├дngers; So gebet bald ihm m├дnnerreiche Habe die nie ein andrer neidisch ihm verk├╝rze.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe swift-moving Maruts are like rapid horses, shining like men gazing at a festival innocent as childrenin the (paternal) mansion, frolicsome as calves, they are the dispensers of water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Maruts, well directed like racehorsesтАФthe young bloods beautify themselves to look like wondrous apparitions;
they are beautiful like children who live in a grand house, playful like calves still suckling.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each p─Бda in this vs. contains a simile marked by n├б comparing the Maruts to domestic animals (a, d), spirits (b), and children (c). Except in c, the simile begins the p─Бda. The vs. contains only one finite verb, ┼Ыubh├бyanta, in b; the functional role of the finite verb is filled instead by the adjectives that are the point of 85 contact between the simile and the frame. In the published translation I deliberately failed to render ab as the rel. cl. it technically is because the тАЬwhich Maruts тАж they тАжтАЭ structure would have intruded upon the succession of similes.

In b opinion is divided on the sense of yakс╣гa-dс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы-. Geldner takes -dс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы- as active, with the first member in an acc. relationship with it (тАЬGeisterseherтАЭ), flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa. in his analysis of the syntax of the cmpd., though not of the meaning of the first member.

So also Renou However, Geldner considers the possibility of a pass. sense in his n. (16b), and Oldenberg opts for the pass. interpr. For disc. of this cmpd. see Scarlatta (232); of his choices I opt for the bahuvr─лhi.

Another oblation to the Maruts at the S─Бkamedha, besides the Gс╣Ыhamedha mentioned above (vs. 14), is made to the kr─лс╕Нin- (тАШplayfulтАЩ) Maruts on the 2nd day of the sacrifice (see, e.g., ┼ЪB II: 20 and Eggeling, SBE XII.408). The characterization of them in d as prakr─лс╕╖├нnaс╕е obviously makes ref. to this oblation.

Griffith

The Maruts, fleet as coursers, while they deck them like youths spectators of a festal meeting,
Linger, like beauteous colts, about the dwelling, like frisking calves, these who pour down the water.

Geldner

Die Marut, die von sch├╢nem Gange wie Rennpferde, die J├╝nglinge, die sich aufputzen wie Geisterseher, sie sind schmuck wie die Kinder in einem vornehmen Hause, wie K├дlber spielend, die Milch saugen und Wasser bringen.

Grassmann

Die Maruts, die wie sch├╢ngeschm├╝ckte Rosse, wie feur’ge Blitze funkeln, sie, die M├дnner, Wie sch├╢ne Kinder in dem Haus sich tummelnd, wie K├дlber springend, wenn sie Milch gesogen.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджрд╢рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реБрдореЗрдХреЗ рд╕реБрд░реВрдкреЗ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдорд╣рд┐рдореНрдирд╛ рдкреВрд░рдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдореГрд│рдиреНрддреБ рдореГрд│рдпрдиреНрддреБред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдЦрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдиреН рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╕рд╡рдГ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдХрд╛ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдЧреЛрд╣рд╛ рдЧрд╡рд╛рдВ рдореЗрдШрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдореБрджрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднреЗрджрдХрдГ рдиреГрд╣рд╛ рдиреГрдгрд╛рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╣рдиреНрддрд╛ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорджреАрдпрдВ рд╡рдзрдГ рдЖрдпреБрдзрдореН рдЖрд░реЗ рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрддреЛ рджреВрд░реЗ рднрд╡рддреБ ред рдпреВрдпрдордкрд┐ рд╕реБрдореНрдиреЗрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрдореНрдиреИрдГ рд╕реБрдЦреИрдГ рд╕рд╣ рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рд╕реБ рдирдордзреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореЗрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдореБрдЦрд╛ рднрд╡рдд рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the munificent Maruts, filling the beautiful heaven and earth with their glory, make us happy; yourfatal weapon, the render of clouds, the destroyer of men, be far from us; bend down to us, Vasus, with blessings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Showing favor, let the Maruts be merciful to us, as they make the two well-fixed world-halves spacious.
Let your cow-smiting, man-smiting weapon stay at a distance. With benevolent thoughts bow to us, good ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. has the feel of a final vs. Though there is no overt sign of a break with what follows, the next vs. turns its attention to the Hotar, Agni, and this might be taken as a change of subject.

In the cadence of p─Бda a mс╣Ыс╕╖antu should be read with a light root syllable, contrary to normal practice. Oldenberg doubts that the form should be read with this exceptional light syllable and ascribes the irregularity to тАЬdie metrische UnebenheitтАЭ of this hymn, while Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition do accept the light reading and adduce one other occurrence that requires this scansion (IV.3.3, though that passage looks more equivocal to me).

Geldner and Renou take varivasy├б-, lit. тАШmake wide spaceтАЩ, in a general тАШhelp, protectтАЩ sense (e.g., тАЬqui prot├иgent les Deux Mondes bien fix├йsтАЭ). But surely the beneficiaries are us (not the two worlds), and the idea is to make the worlds spacious for us.

Griffith

So may the Maruts help us and be gracious, bringing free room to lovely Earth and Heaven.
Far be your bolt that slayeth men and cattle. Ye Vasus, turn yourselves to us with blessings.

Geldner

Die Marut sollen sich uns gef├дllig zeigen und gn├дdig sein, indem sie die beiden festgegr├╝ndeten Welten f├╢rdern. Fern soll eure Rinder und M├дnner mordende Waffe sein. Neiget uns mit Wohlwollen zu, ihr Guten!

Grassmann

Uns reich beschenkend seien hold die Maruts, uns weit und frei die reichen Welten machend; Der Pfeil sei fern, der Rind und M├дnner t├╢dtet, o gute, neigt euch uns mit eurer Gunst zu.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraising your universal liberality, Maruts, the ministrant priest repeatedly worships you, seated (in thesacrificial chamber); he, showerers (of benefits), who is the guardian of the zealous (worshipper), he (the priest),who is void of insincerity, glorifies you with hymns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Hotar, once installed, keeps calling for your giving to be completely directed hither, Maruts, while he is himself being hymned.
He who is the herdsman of such (wealth), o bulls, without duplicity he calls upon you with solemn words.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich of this vs. presents us with a common problem: the most obvious way to interpr. it meets a syntactic stumbling block that should not allow that interpr., and the standard interpr. ignore that obstruction. In this case the issue is the middle participle gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е. This part. is attested over 50x; the vast majority of these attestations are clearly passive in value. In fact, Grassmann interpr. only 2 forms as тАЬmedialтАЭ (that is, transitive, not passive): this passage and I.181.9.

Nonetheless, both Geldner and Renou take it as transitive here (though with different objects) without comment. But I think we ignore the use of the overwhelming majority of forms at our peril. In fact, since Agni as Hotar is the implicit subject of the sentence, a passive value of gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е is easily possible: as both Hotar and god, Agni performs a ritual invocation (as priest) while himself being hymned (as god). (The other 86 occurrence flagged by Grassmann as non-passive, I.181.9, is indeed transitive, but owes its anomalous usage to special circumstances. See comm. ad loc.) If we eliminate gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е as a potential governor of an object, the acc. satr─Б╠Бc─лс╣Г r─Бt├нm must be construed with ─Б╠БтАж johav─лti. Although the acc. with (─Б╠Б) тИЪhv─Б is more usually a god or other animate being, abstract entities (like тАШgivingтАЩ here) are also possible. The vaс╕е in 2nd position in p─Бda a, which might have served as acc. to ─Б╠БтАж johav─лti must then be a gen. dependent on the acc. NP. The more usual configuration is restored in p─Бda d havate vaс╕е тАЬhe calls upon you,тАЭ a minor ex. of poetic repair.

In c both Geldner and Renou supply тАШsacrificerтАЩ with gen. ─л╠Бvataс╕е тАШsuchтАЩ, while I supply тАШwealthтАЩ. There is in fact no good support for either position that I can find. I prefer mine because тАШwealthтАЩ would pick up тАШgivingтАЩ from the previous p─Бda, whereas there is no mention of a sacrificer anywhere. But I do not strongly favor my solution.

gop─Б╠Б- тАШherdsmanтАЩ is regularly construed with с╣Ыt├бsya тАШtruthтАЩ (e.g., I.163.5, III.10.2), so perhaps that phrase is meant, anticipating ├бdvay─Бv─л тАШwithout duplicityтАЩ in d. Note that the gop─Б╠Б- is also ├бdabdha-/ ├бdabhya- тАШundeceivableтАЩ (e.g., II.9.6, X.25.7).

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, vs. 17 тАЬfeelsтАЭ like a final (or pseudo-final) vs. If vs. 18 marks a new beginning, we can note both that in vs. 18 the Hotar invokes the gods as he would at the beginning of a sacrifice and that in vs. 19 (and 20a) the Maruts are referred to four times (19a, b, c, 20a) with the near-deictic pronoun im├й тАЬthese right here,тАЭ which might indicate their epiphany on the ritual ground.

Griffith

The priest, when seated, loudly calls you, Maruts, praising in song your universal bounty.
He, Bulls! who hath so much in his possession, free from duplicity, with hymns invokes you.

Geldner

Der Hotri erfleht, nachdem er sich gesetzt hat, preisend eure vereinte Gabe, ihr Marut. Er, der H├╝ter eines Opferers gleich diesem, ruft euch aufrichtig mit Lobliedern an, ihr Bullen.

Grassmann

Euch ruft herbei der Priester auf dem Sitze, und preist euch an die mannichfache Gabe; Auch er, der solchen Mann besch├╝tzt, o Helden, er ruft euch an mit Spr├╝chen ohne Falschheit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese, Maruts, give plural asure to the zealous (worshipper); these humble the strength of the strong man;they entertain severe displeasure towards the withholder of offerings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These Maruts here bring the hasty to a halt; they make might bow to might.
They protect the laud from the rapacious; they establish heavy hatred for the ungenerous.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was noted above, this vs. contains three examples of the near-deictic im├й, opening the first three p─Бdas. The published translation only fully renders the first one, as three examples of тАЬthese hereтАЭ seemed too heavy. It is also worth noting that, though the im├й forms might suggest the presence of the Maruts right here at the sacrifice (as was suggested above), the clauses in which they are found describe general activities of those gods, which would almost necessarily be performed away from the ritual ground.

Both Geldner and Renou follow the Pp. reading s├бhasaс╕е. Renou interpr. it rather loosely as an abl., whereas Geldner takes it as a gen. and as if it were the differently accented poss.

adj. *sah├бsaс╕е (тАЬdie Gewalt des GewaltigenтАЭ), without comment. Oldenberg suggests that the better reading is dat. s├бhase and cites passages containing ─Б╠БтИЪnam with the dat. I follow this interpr.

18-19 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, vs. 17 тАЬfeelsтАЭ like a final (or pseudo-final) vs. If vs. 18 marks a new beginning, we can note both that in vs. 18 the Hotar invokes the gods as he would at the beginning of a sacrifice and that in vs. 19 (and 20a) the Maruts are referred to four times (19a, b, c, 20a) with the near-deictic pronoun im├й тАЬthese right here,тАЭ which might indicate their epiphany on the ritual ground.

Griffith

These Maruts bring the swift man to a stand-still, and strength with mightier strength they break and humble
These guard the singer from the man who hates him and lay their sore displeasure on the wicked.

Diese Marut d├дmpfen den M├дchtigeren; sie beugen die Gewalt des Gewaltigen. Sie sch├╝tzen die heilige Rede vor dem Neidischen. Dem Geizigen schaffen sie schwere Feindschaft.

Grassmann

Den raschen bringen sie zum Stehn, die Maruts, sie beugen jede Kraft durch eigne St├дrke; Den S├дnger sch├╝tzen vor dem k├╝hnen Feind sie und werfen jede Feindschaft auf den Kargen.

Elizarenkova

рдЗрдореЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд░рдзреНрд░рдВ рдЪрд┐рддреН рд╕рдореГрджреНрдзрдордкрд┐ рдЬрдирдВ рдЬреБрдирдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ред рднреГрдорд┐рдВ рдЪрд┐рддреН рднреНрд░рдордгрд╢реАрд▓рдордкрд┐ рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рдВ рдЬреБрдирдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд╕рд╡рдГ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдХрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдпрдерд╛ рдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрдд рдХрд╛рдордпреЗрд░рдиреН рд╣реЗ рд╡реГрд╖рдгрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдГ рддреЗ рдпреВрдпрдВ рддрдорд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдЕрдк рдмрд╛рдзрдзреНрд╡рдВ рдирд╛рд╢рдпрдд ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рддреЛрдХрдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рддрдирдпрдВ рдкреМрддреНрд░рдВ рдЪ рдзрддреНрдд рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдд рее рее реирелрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese, Maruts, encourage the prosperous man; they encourage the (poor) wanderer; they, as Vasus,are plural ased (with you); showerers (of benefits), dissipate the darkness; grant us many sons and grandsons.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These Maruts here spur on even the feeble, likewise also the whirlwind, in whatever way the good ones please.
Thrust aside the dark shades, o bulls. Confer all life and lineage on us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou both take b as a self-contained clause. I think it better (with MM├╝ller in SBE) to take bhс╣Ы╠Бmiс╣Г cid beginning b as obj. to junanti in p─Бda a, parallel to radhr├бс╣Г cid – beginning a new clause with y├бth─Б in the middle of b. The point would be that the Maruts are so vigorous that they can energize both an entity that has no energy at all (тАЬthe feebleтАЭ) and one that has energy in excess (a whirlwind).

Griffith

These Maruts rouse even the poor and needy: the Vasus love him as an active champion.
Drive to a distance, O ye Bulls, the darkness: give us full store of children and descendants.

Geldner

Diese Marut ermutigen selbst den Schwachen, wie die Guten sich auch am ├Ьbereifrigen freuen. Vertreibet, ihr Bullen, die Finsternis; gebet uns allen leiblichen Samen!

Grassmann

Den Matten auch ermuntern diese Maruts, damit des regen sich die guten freuen; O treibt hinweg die Finsterniss, ihr Stiere, und gebet viele Kinder uns und Enkel.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNever, Maruts, may we be excluded from your bounty; let us not, lords of chariots, be last in itsapportionment; make us sharers in that desirable opulence which, showerers (of benefit), is born of you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let us not miss out on your gift, o Maruts; let us not lag behind at the distribution, o charioteers.
Give us a share in the goods we crave, whatever you have of good quality, o bulls.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The adj. suj─Бt├б- тАШwell-bornтАЩ generally refers to gods, or at least to mortals; it is only here used of material goods (implicitly vasavy├а- in the preceding p─Бda, hence my тАШof good qualityтАЩ. Of course, it is possible that vasavy├а- here refers, at least partly, to human capital (sons), as apparently in II.9.5 ubh├бyam te n├б kс╣г─лyate vasavy├аm … krdhi p├бti ╠е с╣Г svapaty├бsya r─Бy├бс╕е, where the second category of тАЬgoods of both typesтАЭ (ubh├бyam тАж vasavy├аm) is тАЬwealth in good descendentsтАЭ (svapaty├бsya r─Бy├бс╕е). But I donтАЩt think this is a necessary interpr.: тАЬwell-born/producedтАЭ is likely available to semantic extension. 87

Griffith

Never, O Maruts, may we lose your bounty, nor, car-borne Lords! be hitidmost when ye deal it.
Give us a share in that delightful treasure, the genuine wealth that, Bulls! is your possession.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen heroic men, filled with wrath, assemble for (the sake of conquering) many plural nts and people;then, Maruts, sons of Rudra, be our defenders in battles against our enemies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Many plural nts: bahviс╣гu oс╣гadhiс╣гuvikс╣гu = mahat─лс╣гu oс╣гadhiс╣гu praj─Бsu jetavy─Бsu, in great plural nts and people to be subdued; by plural nta orvegetables, oс╣гadhi, the reference is, perhaps, to cultivated lands

Jamison Brereton

When the peoples, the champions clash together in frenzies at (contests for) the boisterous (rivers), the plants, and the clans,
then, o Maruts, Rudriyas, become our rescuers in the battles with the stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As most interpr. point out, the three locc. in b are especially contested objects for the ─Аrya. See esp. Proferes (98): тАЬBecause of their economic value, rivers, plants and clans were subject to competing claims, and constituted flashpoints for conflict between various groups for whom control over resources meant increased powerтАЭ – as well as his elucidation of the three terms. See also Thieme (Fremdling 55), Oberlies (I.350).

Fem. yahv─л╠Б- тАШexuberantтАЩ is in the pl. typed for rivers/waters.

Griffith

What time the men in fury rush together for running streams, for pastures, and for houses.
Then, O ye Maruts, ye who spring from Rudra, be our protectors in the strife with foemen.

Geldner

Wenn die V├╢lker ingrimmig aufeinander schlagen, die Tapferen um Fl├╝sse, Pflanzen, Ansiedlungen, dann seid uns, ihr Rudras├╢hne Marut, Retter im Kampfe um den hohen Herrn!

Grassmann

Wenn zornerf├╝llt die Menschen sich bek├дmpfen um Strombesitz, um Wiesen und um H├дuser, Dann seid, o Maruts, Sch├╝tzer uns in Schlachten, o Rudras├╢hne, wider alle Feinde.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have bestowed, Maruts, many (benefits) on our forefathers, which praiseworthy (benefits) havebeen celebrated in former times; by the (favour of the) Maruts the fierce (warrior) is victorious in combats; by the(favour of the) Maruts the worshipper ever obtains food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Marudbhir it sanit─Б v─Бjam arv─Б: arv─Б = stotrairabhigant─Б, one who overcomes by praises; or, a horse; through the Maruts a horse is the obtainer (of success)in war

Jamison Brereton

Maruts, you have given rise to many solemn speeches from the Forefathers, which have been recited to you long since: along with the Maruts the strong one is the victor in battles; just along with the Maruts does the charger win the prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite the use of тИЪkс╣Ы тАШmakeтАЩ (2nd pl. pf. cakra), it is not likely that the Maruts created the ukth─Б╠Бni themselves, though they are singers on other occasions; rather they provided the occasion and the subject for the poets of earlier eras to celebrate them. Though RenouтАЩs тАШprovokeтАЩ is a bit strong, itтАЩs the right idea. My тАШhave given rise toтАЩ is a bit weak.

Full many a deed ye did for our forefathers worthy of lauds which, even of old, they sang you.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay our male progeny, Maruts, be vigorous, one who is intelligent, the scatterer of (hostile) men, bywhom we may cross the water (of enmity) to a secure dwelling; may we, your (servants), dwell in our own abode.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Beside us let there be a forceful hero, o Maruts, who is lord and apportioner for the people,
with whom we might cross over the waters to good dwelling. Then,
(thanks to) you, might we dominate our own home.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense of p─Бda d is somewhat unclear and the various tr. incompatible.

GeldnerтАЩs тАЬwir m├╢chten euch mehr gelten als das eigene HeimтАЭ seems esp. difficult to wring out of the Skt., though the other possibilities he suggests in the n. (24d) are somewhat more likely. I start with the abh├н тИЪas lexeme, which generally means тАШsurmount, dominate, be superiorтАЩ, which doesnтАЩt seem to be reflected in the Geldner suggestions. However, in my interpr. the enclitic vaс╕е has only the vaguest syntactic connection to the clause. I do not have a better solution.

Griffith

Ours, O ye Maruts, be the vigorous Hero, the Lord Divine of men, the strong Sustainer,
With whom to fair lands we may cross the waters, and dwell in our own home with you beside us.

Geldner

Uns soll, ihr Marut, ein mutiger Held sein, der der Gebieter und Bestimmer der V├╢lker ist, mit dem wir die Gew├дsser zu guter Wohnung ├╝berschreiten wollen. Und wir m├╢chten euch mehr gelten als das eigene Heim.

Grassmann

Bei uns, o Maruts, sei der starke Kriegsheld, der Edle, welcher Gut den Leuten austheilt, Durch den zum Heilsitz wir durchs Wasser schreiten, eur Wohlgefallen m├╢gen wir erlangen.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдХрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ) рдЬрд▓ =рдЬрд▓рд╛рдзрд┐рдкрддрд┐ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ) рдорд┐рддреНрд░ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓ (рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ) рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╡рдирд┐рдирдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрдВ рдЬрд┐рдирдореЗрдВ рдкреЬрддреАрдВ рдРрд╕реЗ рд╡рди рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖ рдЖрджрд┐ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рддрддреН) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрдд рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рдХрд░реНрдо рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рдХреА (рдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрдд) рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рдФрд░ рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН) рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░рдХ рдЧреГрд╣ рдореЗрдВ (рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореН) рдкрд╡рдиреЛрдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рдореАрдк рдореЗрдВ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╕реБрдЦреА (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рдЙрд╕рдореЗрдВ (рдпреВрдпрдореН) рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╕рджрд╛) рд╕рджрд╛ (рдкрд╛рдд) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ реереирелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИ ред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╕рдм рдХреА рдЙрдиреНрдирддрд┐ рдФрд░ рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рджреЛрд╖реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░ рдФрд░ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд╕рдм рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреЛ рд╕рдм рд╕рджрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реереирелрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ, рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛, рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░, рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ, рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдФрд░ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЫрдкреНрдкрдирд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЫрдмреНрдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпрдереЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгреЛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд╛рдк рдУрд╖рдзреАрд░реНрд╡рдирд┐рдиреЛ рдирд╕реНрддрдЬреНрдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрдд рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореБрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрд┐рдирдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рддрддреНрд░ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдирд╕реНрд╕рджрд╛ рдкрд╛рдд реереирелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдХрд┐рдВрд╡рддреН рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрддреН) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рд╡рд╛ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреН (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдзрд┐рдкрддрд┐рдГ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ) рд╕рдЦрд╛ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдГ (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ) рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╡рдирд┐рдирдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдХрд┐рд░рдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рдирд╕реНрдерд╛ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрдпрдГ (рдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрдд) рд╕реЗрд╡рдиреНрддрд╛рдореН (рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН) рд╢рд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░рдХреЗ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рднрд╡реЗрдо (рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореН) рд╡рд╛рдпреВрдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ (рдпреВрдпрдореН) (рдкрд╛рдд) (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) (рд╕рджрд╛) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН реереирелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рджрдпрдГ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдиреБрдиреНрдирдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪ рддрдереИрд╡ рджреЛрд╖рд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢реНрдп рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдиреБрдиреНрдиреАрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╕рджрд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ реереирелрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдорд░реБрджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдЧреБрдгрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрд░реНрдерджрд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рдбреНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ ! рдЬрд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреА рдЙрдиреНрдирддреА рд╡ рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддрд╕реЗ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдВрдЪреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзреА рд╡ рджреЛрд╖рд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реВрди рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реирел рее
